# Financial Modeling Foundations (2018)

> By distilling key information regarding cash flow levels and risks, financial modeling helps decision-makers make informed choices based on data analytics that move their firms forward. In this course, learn how to build financial models that can be used in corporate finance, investment banking, commercial banking, and portfolio management. Professor Michael McDonald covers financial statement mod

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018) | 3h | 322K learners
> [Jump to Path Context ↓](#path-context)

- **1. Introduction** (2 videos)
- **2. 1. Financial Modeling Basics** (8 videos)
- **3. 2. Corporate Financial Modeling: Three-Statement Financial Model** (8 videos)
- **4. 3. Evaluating Corporate Financial Models: Three-Statement Model** (3 videos)
- **5. 4. Investment Models: DCF Model** (4 videos)
- **6. 5. Banking Models** (7 videos)
- **7. 6. Buyout Models** (7 videos)
- **8. 7. Financial Modeling across Industries** (4 videos)
- **9. 8. Building and Maintaining Models** (4 videos)
- **10. Conclusion** (1 videos)

### 1. Introduction

#### Using Excel for financial modeling
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/using-excel-for-financial-modeling?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/using-excel-for-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Mike] Hi there, I'm Mike McDonald.
>
> **[0:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/using-excel-for-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=2)** I'm a professor of finance, a frequent consultant to industry, and a Wall Street veteran.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/using-excel-for-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=7)** In this course on financial modeling, I want to show you how to build financial models for use in corporate finance investments and banking.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/using-excel-for-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=16)** We're going to learn how to do financial forecasts in a model to understand where a firm is headed in the future.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/using-excel-for-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=22)** We're also going to see how we can evaluate financial models to answer important questions for the firm.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/using-excel-for-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=28)** Finally, we're going to learn how to update our models to make them easier to read, avoid problems like circular references, and build in advanced tools like scenario analysis.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/using-excel-for-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=40)** All of this will be done through the lens of Excel, the key tool in finance.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/using-excel-for-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=46)** If you're a premium member, there are exercise files available for the course that'll enrich your learning.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/using-excel-for-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=52)** So if you're ready to start on your way towards a model future in finance, then come with me, and let's begin.

### 2. 1. Financial Modeling Basics

#### What is financial modeling?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] What is Financial Modeling?
>
> **[0:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=2)** At its core, financial modeling is really just a business form of what we call a model.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=9)** So what is a model?
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=10)** Well it's really a simplified representation of reality.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=13)** A map is a great example of this.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=16)** If you think about what a map does, it helps us to simplify reality.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=20)** It tells us how to get from point A to point B, and only focuses on the details we worry about or care about, like what streets to take to get to our destination.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=30)** We avoid all of the unimportant details that we don't care about.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=34)** Things like what tress or buildings are along the way, or what other cars might be around, things like that.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=40)** If we had to represent the full complexity of reality, including trees and buildings, the map would be much more difficult to read.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=50)** A financial model does exactly the same thing.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=53)** Every major company decision is decided based on how much the outcome of that decision is worth.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=59)** Firms need a way to figure out how to make those decisions based on the reality of the world without all the gory detail that's unnecessary, and that's where financial modeling comes in.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=74)** Financial Modeling involves assessing a future level of cash flows for a particular business or project, and then the risks around those cash flows.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=84)** We put these things together, we take our current cash flows in reality, what we project them to be in the future, and then we value those based on the risks to the business.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=96)** That's what a financial model does at its core.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=100)** In particular, when we get done, our financial model should help us to summarize a number of different factors from reality into a single output that we care about.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=111)** The particular output might vary depending on the model or the business, but it could be something like net present value, or internal rate of return.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=120)** It might be the value per share for a company that we're considering buying, or for our own company.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=125)** It might be an internal metric, like debt service coverage.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=129)** Whatever that metric is, the financial model helps us to get there.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=133)** In particular, the financial model lets us focus on the key issues and risks.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=139)** Just like the map helps us go from point A to point B, a financial model lets us take our business from our starting point to our intended destination, without having to worry about unimportant details along the way.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=155)** Now a good financial model then needs to have three characteristics.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=159)** Number one, needs to be simple, but not so simple as to artificially distort reality.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=166)** Number two, it really needs to focus on the key cash flow drivers for the business.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=172)** What are the key factors that drive the business forward?
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=176)** These need to be captured in the model so that decision makers understand them.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=181)** And then third and finally, it needs to convey the assumptions and conclusions that business decision makers care about.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=188)** If we're gonna assume that revenues will grow at 5% on an annual basis going forward, our financial model needs to make that clear.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=196)** There's nothing wrong with making those assumptions as long as they're clearly identified for managers and business decision makers.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=204)** In particular, a good financial model should help us to evaluate risks around a business decision.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=211)** We can use a variety of techniques to evaluate those risks: Sensitivity analysis, break-even analysis, scenario analysis, and more.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=219)** The financial model helps us to understand the risks and complexities of the business decision that we're making.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=226)** There's a variety of alternatives to a traditional financial model.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=231)** For example, business decision makers often rely on gut feeling or back of the envelope calculations.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=237)** These are a great sanity check for a financial model, but they're not a substitute.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=241)** Smart business decision makers know that financial models are an important starting point for most decisions.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=249)** The financial models that we use can be either deterministic or stochastic.
>
> **[4:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=254)** Deterministic models set assumptions and then compute financial ratios and cash flows based on those assumptions.
>
> **[4:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=263)** We can also use stochastic models.
>
> **[4:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=265)** These are really involving a lot more probability theory.
>
> **[4:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=268)** We won't talk about those as much in this course, and they're more complex to implement in reality, so they're not as widely used.
>
> **[4:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=276)** A couple of important notes here: First of all, you can't model what you don't understand.
>
> **[4:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=281)** For that reason, we're making the assumption that you understand something about finance.
>
> **[4:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=287)** If you need a refresher or maybe help with the basics, I recommend two courses here on linked and learn: Excel for Corporate Finance Professions, and Excel for Management Accounting.
>
> **[4:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/what-is-financial-modeling?u=76281980&t=298)** Each of these will give you the background that you need to be able to succeed with financial modeling going forward.

#### Why is financial modeling important?
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/why-is-financial-modeling-important?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/why-is-financial-modeling-important?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Why should you care about financial modeling?
>
> **[0:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/why-is-financial-modeling-important?u=76281980&t=2)** In the next few minutes, I'll explain what financial modeling is, and how understanding it can help you move your career forward.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/why-is-financial-modeling-important?u=76281980&t=10)** For anyone pursuing or advancing a career in corporate development, investment banking, FP&A, also called financial planning and analysis, equity research, commercial banking, or any other area of corporate finance, building financial models is part of the daily routine.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/why-is-financial-modeling-important?u=76281980&t=26)** The reality is that for many of the most lucrative and exciting areas of finance, financial modeling is a critical skill that you need to have.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/why-is-financial-modeling-important?u=76281980&t=36)** In particular, financial modeling is really just a tool to help decision makers make decisions.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/why-is-financial-modeling-important?u=76281980&t=44)** These kinds of decisions include, for example, whether or not to invest in a company, an asset or security, whether or not to pursue a project, like, for example, a new R&D project at a firm, or building a new factory, whether or not to pursue a merger acquisition deal.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/why-is-financial-modeling-important?u=76281980&t=63)** Either to sell the company that you currently work for, or to purchase another company.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/why-is-financial-modeling-important?u=76281980&t=68)** Or whether or not to raise capital from the outside markets.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/why-is-financial-modeling-important?u=76281980&t=72)** All of these kinds of decisions are critical to the future of any company that's out there, and financial modeling is what helps us make those decisions.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/why-is-financial-modeling-important?u=76281980&t=83)** In particular, a good financial model allows decision makers to test scenarios, observe potential outcomes, and hopefully make an informed decision, that's the idea at least.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/why-is-financial-modeling-important?u=76281980&t=94)** Now, the reality is that today, there's a lot of talk about new software programs being used in modeling.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/why-is-financial-modeling-important?u=76281980&t=102)** But, take it from me, based on my experience, and based on the experience of countless other corporate finance professionals, Excel is still the dominant software tool for financial modeling, the vast majority of financial modeling takes place in Excel.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/why-is-financial-modeling-important?u=76281980&t=118)** There was a newspaper report a few months ago about how certain companies were moving away from Excel, and starting to use other software programs in financial modeling, but a follow-up survey to that, and the vast majority of user response to that article showed that Excel is still the dominant tool in this space.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/why-is-financial-modeling-important?u=76281980&t=139)** If you're going to be an effective financial modeler, then, you need to understand Excel, and you need to be able to perform financial models in Excel.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/why-is-financial-modeling-important?u=76281980&t=148)** At this point, hopefully you understand the basics of when and where financial modeling is useful.

#### Business questions and financial models
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Financial modeling lets us evaluate very specific sets of circumstances and make decisions based on those situations.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=8)** Since the kind of decisions we make in business differ under various circumstances, the models that we use to evaluate those decisions differ as well.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=18)** There's a few major types of financial models that you'll encounter in a business setting.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=23)** The first of these is what we call a corporate financial model, or a three statement model.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=29)** The goal in a corporate model or three statement model is just to understand how the firm is performing and how it's expected to perform in the future.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=38)** So it helps us to evaluate where the firm is going if things continue as they have been in the past.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=46)** To build this kind of model, we're gonna use the corporation's history.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=50)** All firms generally have a history unless they're a brand new startup.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=54)** We assume that that corporation will last indefinitely in the future.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=59)** Now that probably won't happen in reality of course, but it does mean that we can make an assumption about the firm's terminal value in the end.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=70)** So we take the firm's historical cash flow figures, project them for a period of time, and then assume that at some point in the future we just wanna have the corporation sold or shut down or closed, and the terminal value is the value at the conclusion of our financial model.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=91)** The second type of financial model we'll encounter is a project finance model.
>
> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=96)** This is typically built around what we call a DCF or discounted cash flow model.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=101)** A project finance decision involves a company looking at a particular investment option.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=109)** Be it a new R and D project, a new piece of equipment, perhaps building a new facility, et cetera.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=114)** All of these different kinds of projects have different phases.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=118)** An investment phase, a revenue generation phase, and then a closing phase.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=124)** So we buy a new piece of equipment for example, we have to install that equipment, it operates for a while, and then eventually the equipment wears out, and we throw it away or scrap it or sell it.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=135)** So we have no history in the case of a DCF model.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=139)** Instead we're just gonna focus on our projected cash flows of the future, and we're gonna project them throughout the entire history of that particular project or investment.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=150)** And that'll let us make a decision about whether this investment is a good choice or a bad choice.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=155)** Third, we have what we call a leverage buyout model.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=159)** Leveraged buyout models are closely related to M and A or merger and acquisition models.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=164)** These kinds of models involve a defining transaction for a company.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=170)** One company buying another.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=172)** These have important characteristics.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=174)** For example, what is the purchase price for the acquired company?
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=178)** What's the holding period for this company investment?
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=181)** And then do we sell or exit that investment in the future?
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=185)** These kinds of models need to show how any alternative financing sources are repaid.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=191)** Are we borrowing money from the bank?
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=192)** Or issuing bonds, perhaps.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=195)** Those kinds of financing decisions need to be taken into account by the model.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=200)** We also need to demonstrate the return earned by an equity investor.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=205)** Following up on an M and A model, we have what we call an integrated consolidation model.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=210)** These will compute the earnings per share and other financial ratios before and after an acquisition.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/business-questions-and-financial-models?u=76281980&t=216)** And this lets us get a better handle on whether that acquisition was successful, and whether or not we have successfully combined the two companies as we initially intended to.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>

> **Tools:** terminal (2)
> **Definitions:** is a  (2)

#### Data for a model
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Effective financial modeling is driven by data, but different types of models require different kinds of data.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=7)** In the next couple of minutes, I'll show you how to determine what data you will need to build an effective financial model.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=14)** All businesses have access to lots of data.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=17)** There's a variety of different sources of data that you can use when it's time to start gathering data to build a financial model.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=25)** You'll probably have access to proprietary data, like customer data, for example, you certainly have access to publicly available data, for example from the U.S. Census Bureau or the Federal Reserve.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=37)** But you probably want to start with internal data.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=40)** Most financial models begin with internal data, for example, data about historical financials for the firm, revenue, costs, profits, et cetera.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=53)** You wanna build in some external data for scenario analysis, though, or where you are trying to model something that's particularly complicated, and where external factors may play a big role on the outcome the company sees.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=67)** So where can you get the data you need?
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=69)** You have three choices: buy it, build it, or gather it.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=75)** Those are the three options to get any piece of data that you need, and they're the only three options.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=81)** If you're going to buy data, there's a variety of vendors out there that you can choose from, depending on the type of data that you need.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=88)** Building data is more difficult, but it won't necessarily cost your company any money directly.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=94)** If you're trying to build a data set, you might, for example, be able to rely on internal data the company already has, or at least be able to build data based on an existing customer base, your CRM, et cetera.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=107)** And then finally, you can gather data from a variety of public sources to build your data set.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=113)** So, what type of data do you need for the project?
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=117)** Well, that's the key question in any financial model.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=120)** Your data needs are driven by your project needs.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=123)** So ask yourself, what are you trying to model?
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=126)** Is this a short-term financial model, meaning less than a year, or is it a long-term financial model over multiple years?
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=133)** Is this a model where external factors are gonna play a major role in the decision making process?
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=140)** If so, you probably want external data about the marketplace and competitors.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=145)** Or is this primarily an internal financial model, where success or failure of the decision will be driven by internal decisions made by the company.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=154)** In that case, you may not need any external data at all.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=157)** So start by thinking about what you're trying to model, and then ask yourself what the characteristics are of that decision, and that'll tell you what data you need for your project.
>
> **[2:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/data-for-a-model?u=76281980&t=169)** Now you're ready to start identifying and collecting data specific to your firm and its particular needs and issues.

#### Sources of data
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Identifying the data you need for a financial model is just the first step.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=4)** You also need to actually go out there and gather that data from various sources.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=9)** Fortunately, this is easier than it once was.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=12)** Thanks to some great tools and databases that are available online.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=17)** Traditionally, one big issue for firms in complex financial models was the lack of external data.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=24)** You usually had to pay for that data that could be very expensive.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=27)** Today, there's a variety of great sources for free external data.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=32)** Three top sources you'll wanna consider, depending on what you're trying to model, are the BLS or Bureau of Labor Statistics, The Fed or Federal Reserve, and the U.S. Census Bureau.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=42)** Each of these has different data sets that you could use depending on the financial model that you're trying to build.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=50)** For something like in the model of how your company's labor costs will change over time and as a result how your profits will change over time, BLS data might be more helpful.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=63)** For conditions related to the financial system as a whole and perhaps the economy, Federal Reserve data is more likely to be more helpful.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=70)** And for issues related to your customers and your market share, and your ability to raise prices, data on those customers from the U.S. Census Bureau might be key.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=82)** In addition you can also gather data on non traditional metrics that you might care about.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=88)** Google Trends has a variety of different kinds of data related to searches that are done through its search engines.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=97)** This is great data to use in a variety of different scenarios.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=104)** Now, in addition to external data that you could gather, if you want data on specific industries or competitors, there's a good chance that you're gonna have to buy it.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=115)** In particular, buying that data is most realistic if we're talking about gathering data specific to a particular industry and the competition we face in that industry.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=128)** Be aware, though, that it can be very expensive to buy this kind of data.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=131)** So make sure that it's data that you really and truly need for the project in question.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=137)** An alternative to buying data can be surveys.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=141)** There's a variety of new online tools for conducting surveys.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=145)** And this gives you the ability to get data on OPCs, other people's customers.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=151)** Understand what it is your competitors are doing that you're not doing and then how that will influence your market share over time.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=159)** The key, though, is to understand what kind of biases you introduce by using a survey.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=165)** Remember, any survey that you do needs to be representative of the rest of the world.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=171)** So if you're trying to figure out how to sell to other customers or new customers you need to ask yourself if the existing customers you're surveying are representative of your target customers.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sources-of-data?u=76281980&t=182)** Now you should have a handle on where to go to get data in general for a financial model you might wanna construct.

#### Gathering data from FRED for Excel
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=1)** - [Narrator] While many financial models may not require special data, some do.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=5)** In particular, if you're making projections about the future, or about the level of market share a firm will have, it's helpful to have outside data as part of that process.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=15)** You can often get this data through Excel.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=19)** In particular, I'm gonna show you how to use a tool called "FRED" to do this.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=23)** Now FRED, or the Federal Reserve Economic Database, is available for free from the St. Louis Federal Reserve.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=31)** You will need to download a special free Excel add-in, and generally you'll want to use the Excel 2013 version.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=38)** Go ahead and download that Excel add-in, and you'll be ready to use it.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=44)** Once you're in Excel, you're prepared to begin downloading data from FRED, but to do this, you need to install the add-in.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=51)** So you'll want to go to File, then down to Options, come over to Add-Ins, and then come down to Manage Excel Add-Ins and click Go.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=66)** Once you'll do that, you'll see a variety of different add-ins you can use, but you won't have FRED just yet.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=73)** You need to figure out where you've downloaded that FRED add-in to.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=79)** Typically you'll find the FRED add-in in your Downloads folder.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=84)** Go ahead and add that add-in, then click OK.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=89)** Once you do this, you should see a new tab pop up at the top that says FRED.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=94)** Now FRED is great because it gives you the ability to directly download data into Excel for a variety of different areas you might be interested in.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=103)** Let's pretend that we're doing a financial model related to auto sales.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=108)** Well we could go and buy data from someone like Hoovers for example, or Merchant, but we could also get data related to auto sales from the federal reserve.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=119)** If we click Browse Popular US Data, we'll see a variety of different types of data that we might be interested in.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=126)** Everything from production and business activity data, like industrial production numbers or housing starts, to data on payroll, job openings, number of hours worked, data on gross domestic product, and other overall national level indicators to the health of the economy.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=145)** And of course data on inflation and money supply.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=149)** We even have data available internationally, from a variety of major countries around the world.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=155)** Now, let's go ahead and download some data that might be useful to us in certain settings.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=163)** For example, maybe we're trying to do some sort of an analysis related to future market share around a company that's in the automobile business.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=174)** Well, wouldn't it be helpful to understand how fast auto sales are growing over time?
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=179)** To do that, we can download data on like-vehicle sales, and we'll add to that perhaps a couple other factors that we care about.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=188)** So maybe we are also interested in, for example, inflation... And perhaps we're interested in oil prices.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=199)** As I clicked each of these different indicator variables that we're interested in, you'll notice that an acronym, or pneumonic, popped up in the top of the column.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=209)** That's the code that tells FRED which data point we're interested in.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=213)** Once we have this data, we're ready to click "get FRED data" and now the data will auto-fill over time.
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=222)** This shows us, for example, the level of automobile sales in millions of units sold each month from 1976 through 2018.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=236)** Now, maybe we're not interested in going back as far as 1976.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=240)** Perhaps we want to start with 1990 data for each of these different variables.
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=244)** To do that, we'll change the year in the date shown in row four for each column.
>
> **[4:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=252)** So I'm going to change automobile sales from starting in 1900, or as early as the data is available, to starting in 1990.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=261)** I'll do the same thing in column C, in cell C4, which will tell me about inflationary data, and then again in E4, as it relates to oil prices.
>
> **[4:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=275)** Once I do this, I can click "get FRED data" and all of my data now updates so that it starts in 1990 and goes through present time in 2018.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/gathering-data-from-fred-for-excel?u=76281980&t=289)** At this point, you should understand how to use FRED to pull in outside data that's relevant to your financial modeling needs.

#### Getting started with the project
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Building a financial model requires getting your hands dirty by actually demonstrating what will happen in a scenario, using figures and projections in Excel.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=8)** Throughout this course, I will try to keep us all on the same page by using partially prebuilt Excel examples.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=14)** Let's dive in to one of those examples, shall we?
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=17)** I'm in the 01_07.Begin Excel file.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=22)** Now what you're going to see here is that we have an income statement, a balance sheet, and a statement of cash flows for a firm.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=30)** All three of these are linked together based on different formulas.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=35)** So some portions of any financial statements will be driven by data from the firm, something like COGS, as an example, or SG&A, particularly on a historical basis.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=45)** These won't be projections or calculations; they'll be derived directly from what the firm actually reports.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=51)** Other items, like Operating Income or Net Income, might be derived from various subsections of the income statement, the balance sheet, or the cashflow statement.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=62)** Moreover, when we look at the cashflow statement, this in essence reconciles the income statement and the balance sheet with the cash balances of the company.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=72)** Thus it's frequently going to draw from the other two statements.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=77)** This is the beauty of a three-statement financial model.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=81)** In this particular case, we're making various assumptions about what's going to happen to the firm over time, but most of our items are drawn directly from other places in the financial statements.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=95)** A good financial model needs to have clean, clear linkages between all three of your financial statements so that it's easy for outsiders to read.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=105)** When we get done, we should be able to understand what's happened to that firm over time based on the financials.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=114)** In the case of this particular firm, we can see that the firm has a rapidly increasing cash balance.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=121)** They're holding a lot of cash on hand, and they're growing very rapidly.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=125)** The nice thing about doing all of this in Excel is that if we were to go through and change any of these numbers, let's say we were to adjust out net income from the income statement, it should dynamically update across all of our other financial statements.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=143)** And that's exactly what we see.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=145)** So our ending cash balance is adjusted based on the change that we made in the income statement to net income.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/getting-started-with-the-project-2?u=76281980&t=153)** At this point, you should have a good grasp on the mechanics of financial statement linkages and how different data points fit together through formulas in Excel.

#### Excel tips for financial modeling
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Financial modeling is really as much an art as it is a science, but there are some basic tips that you should adhere to when you're building financial models.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=9)** First of all, you need to understand that Excel is the main tool used by a variety of institutions, banks, corporations, et cetera, to really do financial modeling.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=18)** And the reason for this is that it's so versatile.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=22)** Excel can be tailored to whatever the specific situations or needs are of the company and the financial model they're trying to build.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=30)** That's both its benefit and its drawback.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=33)** There are no rules or checks in place to ensure accuracy unless you build them in.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=39)** For that reason, you want to adhere to some common rules that are broadly used across industry.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=45)** Try to color code your data so that you can distinguish between inputs and formulas.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=52)** For example, maybe use blue and black for one and the other.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=55)** Try to incorporate your standalone three-statement model on a single worksheet.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=60)** Don't separate it into different sheets or it becomes harder to read.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=64)** Then, go through and separate your assumptions and drivers from the rest of the model.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=69)** Have a section at the top so that anyone reviewing that model can easily go through and review what assumptions you've made.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=76)** Moreover, you want to go through and use clear headers and subheaders with something like bold shading, as an example, so that people can follow what's going on in your model.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=86)** Where needed, include comments to help people to understand the assumptions that you're making or why you're doing various calculations.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=94)** It's also helpful to go in and put in error checks to ensure that your balance sheet balances, as an example, or to ensure that you're not making some sort of an error in moving from one period to another.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=107)** Moreover, you want to make sure that users can follow where that information is coming from and the logic for the model.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=115)** So make sure that you're being consistent with your formulas over time.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=119)** And certainly, avoid linking to other Excel workbooks unless absolutely necessary.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=124)** It's very, very hard to follow what goes on if you're linking to third-party sources.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=129)** Similarly, circular references are very common in financial models.
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=135)** You want to avoid them unless it's absolutely necessary.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=138)** The problem it becomes that those circular references create a real headache if you want to change anything, and they can actually create inaccurate output.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=146)** Finally, consider using tables, charts, and graphics to summarize any important information.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/excel-tips-for-financial-modeling-2?u=76281980&t=152)** Follow these steps and your models will be much more effective and easier for outside users to evaluate.

> **Code Keywords:** finally, (1)
> **Definitions:** is a  (1)

### 3. 2. Corporate Financial Modeling: Three-Statement Financial Model

#### Foundations of the model
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Presenter] The art of financial modeling, mostly relates to making assumptions about the future performance of the business being modeled.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=7)** This is the most subjective, but also the most important part in valuation of a firm.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=13)** In particular, there's four different types of Financial Forecasts that are used.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=18)** It's critical that we understand these different methods of financial forecasting, because, again, that's the crux, that is the meat and potatoes, of our financial model.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=29)** If we get the forecast wrong, our model will inherently be wrong.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=33)** Now, the reality is that that financial modeling, really is an art form.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=38)** We're making assumptions about the future performance of the business.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=42)** And that can be difficult to do.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=44)** Because this is the subjective part of valuation, it's an area where reasonable minds can differ.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=51)** There's no truly right answer, but there are wrong answers.
>
> **[0:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=55)** A growth rate of five percent next year, or six percent, either one could be right for your company.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=61)** A growth rate of 500 percent is probably not right.
>
> **[1:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=65)** Either way, forecasting is critical to modeling.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=69)** Now, as I said, there's four different types of financial forecasts.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=72)** The first is what we call Top-Down Analysis.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=75)** This starts with our total addressable market, and then works its way down.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=80)** So, for example, you might start by thinking about what is the company's market share, and then what is its share in different geographic segments?
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=88)** What is the share based on products that are out there, and the product the company sells?
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=93)** And then, how much can they rely on for revenue from each particular customer?
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=97)** How much will a customer buy in a given period of time?
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=100)** We can then get to revenues once we have all that information.
>
> **[1:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=104)** We take our market share, multiply it by the size of the market, for a particular product, and by the sales per customer, and we get a sense for what our revenues are overall.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=115)** The second type of financial forecast is a Bottoms-Up Analysis.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=119)** This starts with the basic drivers of the business.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=121)** So, for example, if you're an ecommerce firm, you'd start with your website traffic.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=126)** And then build on that: if a million people come to the website every month, well what's our conversion rate then?
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=133)** If one percent of those people convert and buy something, that's 10,000 people.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=138)** Now what's the value of what they purchase?
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=141)** If that is ten dollars per customer, on average, well 10,000 customers buy, and they purchase an average of ten dollars per order, that gives us $100,000 in revenue.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=154)** Your top-down forecast, and your bottoms-up analysis should come up with the same number, in theory.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=160)** It might differ a little bit based on the assumptions, but if you're coming up with dramatically different numbers, that means you're doing something wrong.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=167)** The third method of financial forecasting is a little bit more sophisticated, and less subjective.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=172)** It's called Regression Analysis.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=175)** Regression analysis involves analyzing the relationship between two variables.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=181)** For example, we might be interested in understanding how other external factors impact the revenue of our firm.
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=189)** How does our marketing spend?
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=190)** Or our price compared to our competitor's impact our revenue?
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=195)** If we gather the appropriate data, we can then make a very clean scientific forecast about what our revenues, or profits, or any other variable would be going forward.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=205)** Typically, you can perform a regression analysis in Excel, but again it's a little bit more advanced.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=212)** Finally, the most basic type of forecasting, simply using a Year-Over-Year Growth Rate, often called a CAGR.
>
> **[3:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=219)** That's what we're gonna do throughout this course.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=221)** The reality is that even though this is the most basic type of forecasting, it's still very commonly used in industry.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=228)** In part, because it's simple and easy to understand.
>
> **[3:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=231)** You can build a financial model around any of these four types of financial forecasts, but most of the time, you'll see CAGRs used as a starting point, and then you might go to more advanced models as needed.
>
> **[4:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=243)** The more advanced forecasting techniques are not a major focus of this course.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=248)** If you're interesting in learning more, and I think it's a great thing to do that, then I recommend two other courses here on LinkedIn Learning: Financial Forecasting with Big Data, and Applied Economic Forecasting with Big Data.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/foundations-of-the-model?u=76281980&t=261)** Now that you have a hand on the different types of financial forecasts used in modeling, we're ready to proceed.
