#### Linking financial statements
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The first step in many financial models is linking the different financial statements together.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=5)** In point of fact, this actually seems trivial.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=7)** It doesn't seem too hard to put together the income statement with the balance sheet, right.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=11)** But in reality it can be a lot trickier than you might think.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=16)** Let's see how it's done.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=17)** Let's take a look at the steps, shall we.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=19)** So, step one in linking the financial statements, is to begin by calculating our revenue.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=25)** We're gonna do this based on some kind of a forecasting approach.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=29)** From there, you need to go through and fill in your other major accounting statement items, so cost of goods sold or COGs, your gross profit, your operating expenses.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=39)** And then when we get done, you should have your earnings before interest, taxes, depreciation, and amortization, or EBITDA as it's more commonly known.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=49)** Once you've gone through and filled out the financial statement, you're ready to begin creating your supporting schedules.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=56)** In particular, we don't necessarily talk a lot about supporting schedules in accounting.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=61)** They're not as widely used or widely known as the balance sheet, the income statement and the cash flow statement, but they are critical.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=69)** In particular, they're gonna help us to understand the details that are gonna go into each of those major financial statements.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=76)** So you need to create supporting schedules for your capital assets, and this will tell us what our property, plant and equipment, or PP&E, expenses are.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=85)** They'll tell us about depreciation, and our capex, or capital expenditures.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=89)** Then you're gonna have a supporting schedule for your working capital balance.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=93)** This tells us what level of accounts receivable, and accounts payable we expect, and what level of inventory we have on hand.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=99)** Finally, you're gonna have a financing schedule.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=102)** That's gonna tell us, over time, what kind of capital are we raising, is it equity or debt.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=108)** And then what kind of payments do we need to make to that capital in the form of dividends, interest payments, et cetera.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=115)** Once you've finished with step two, you're ready to go through and fill in the income statement.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=120)** In particular, you can now finish up by adding in some of the non-cash expenses, like depreciation.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=126)** And you can also fill out interest and taxes, and that'll leave you with net income.
>
> **[2:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=131)** From there you're prepared to fill in the balance sheet items, everything except for cash.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=137)** Cash is the last part of the financial model that you'll complete.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=141)** Then finally, in step four, you're gonna build out your cash flow statement.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=145)** Look at all the cash from operating activities.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=148)** The cash that's used in, or generated by, investing activities.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=152)** And cash from financing activities.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=154)** You take these three separate components, cash from operations, cash from investing, and cash from financing, put them all together and that'll give you your closing cash balance.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=165)** And that should be linked back to the balance sheet, which let's you complete your financial model.
>
> **[2:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=171)** Now you're prepared to see where the company is going in the weeks, months and years ahead.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/linking-financial-statements?u=76281980&t=178)** At this point, hopefully, you understand how to link the financial statements together to start building a comprehensive picture of the firms financial statement, or at least you understand it in principle.

#### Three-statement financial model
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] One of our first tasks in building out a financial model, especially a three-statement financial model is to go through and evaluate the financial statements and make sure they're complete.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=10)** Now what we have here are three different financial statements for a basic model, the income statement, the balance sheet, and the statement of cashflows.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=21)** We have this on a historical basis for the period 2014 to 2018.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=27)** And while we filled out most of the model, there are certain pieces that are missing, like Operating Income, Income Before Tax, etc.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=35)** We'll need to fill these in using formulas.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=38)** In addition, we have helpful comments added at various points in time that give us a sense for how different figures were arrived at.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=48)** So let's go through and fill out this model, shall we?
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=52)** So for Operating Income, we are going to be basing this on our operating expenses versus our revenue.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=61)** In this particular case, we'll have C22, our Revenue, minus C27, our Unusual Expenses, minus our Total Operating Expenses, C28.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=76)** Once we've calculated this for the first year, we can apply the same formula across all five years of our model.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=83)** It's that easy, right?
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=84)** Similarly, when we want to calculate our income before taxes we'll go through and take our Operating Income and then subtract off our Interest Expense.
>
> **[1:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=95)** Having done that, we can apply it across all five years.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=100)** Now to calculate our Net Income, we're going to use our Income After Taxes plus our Extraordinary Items, and this is where you can see where notes are helpful.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=110)** In this particular case, our Extraordinary Items could have been either negative or positive.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=115)** Here, we've used a simple positive 100 for Net Income.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=119)** We can now apply this across all five years.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=122)** And to determine our normalized earnings per share, we'll take that Net Income divided by the number of shares outstanding, and this gives us the earnings per share on a regular basis.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=137)** We could go through and apply this same principle to the balance sheet to determine our total assets, which will be based on our current assets plus the sum of our various long-term asset components.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=153)** Once we've done that, we'll be able to apply this across all five years.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=158)** We can do the same thing for liabilities, taking our current liabilities and then adding to them all of our components in Long Term Debt, including the recently added Capital Lease Obligations.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=175)** And then finally, we can go through and determine our Equity based on the components above, which will include Common Stock, Additional Paid-in Capital, Retained Earnings, and the Unrealized Gains we have.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/three-statement-financial-model-2?u=76281980&t=194)** Once we've done all that, we may wish to make a couple of cosmetic changes, including adding some borders in Excel, just to make it look a little neater and cleaner, but as you can see, we've been quickly able to build out the rest of our basic three-statement model with minimal trouble, thanks to the power of Excel and the formulas used therein.

#### Setting source parameters
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] While building out the income statement and the balance sheet portion of the three-statement financial model is usually fairly straightforward, building out the statement of cash flows can be a little bit trickier because it often draws from the income statement and the balance sheet.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=14)** I'm in the zero two zero four begin Excel file.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=18)** Now we have our basic three-statement model and this includes the balance sheet and the income statement completely filled out for our purposes.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=26)** But we have a significant portion of the statement of cash flows that's missing.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=32)** In our case though, we should be able to go through and fill out the rest of the sheet based on that income statement and balance sheet.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=40)** Notice the net income portion, which starts the cash from operating activities, this is going to be drawn directly from our income statement above.
>
> **[0:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=50)** So our net income flows right out of the bottom of the income statement.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=56)** We want to make sure that we continue to do this across the entire statement of cash flows.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=62)** Next, we're going to need to go through and add back all of the non-cash items in order to get our total cash from operations.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=72)** So that's going to include, for example, depreciation.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=75)** In this case, we don't have a direct appreciation line in our income statement.
>
> **[1:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=80)** So instead we're going to use the change in accumulated depreciation year to year from the balance sheet.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=88)** We can then follow that approach across all five years.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=92)** The same thing holds true when we look at net receivables.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=97)** We haven't directly tied that out of the income statement, so we're instead going to use the balance sheet in order to determine that particular line item.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=107)** Inventories, as you might expect, will come directly off of the balance sheet.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=114)** But we might wish to use the change in inventories rather than just inventories over time.
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=120)** So we'd want to adjust our formula so that it takes into account the previous year's inventories just as we did with receivables.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=130)** Next, we're looking at changes in working capital.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=133)** This is going to be based on our current assets and current liabilities in each year.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=137)** And again, we're looking at the differences between them in each period.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=143)** Once we've figured all of these particular items we can go through and sum them up in order to get our total cash from operations.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=153)** This'll include all of our changes in working capital, receivables, depreciation, et cetera.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=159)** Next, we'll want to go through and look at our change in cash investing activities.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=165)** This is going to be based on capital expenditures and any sale and purchases of different investments.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=172)** Now, purchases and sales of investments may not appear in other places so in this particular case we're simply going to assume that we have the same level each year on an ongoing basis.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=185)** We'd probably need to gather this data from supporting schedules, which we don't have in this particular set of financial statements.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=193)** For our purposes, I'm just going to assume that those changes are consistent from period to period rather than trying to draw them from other parts of the financial statements.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=204)** Once we've done that, we can go through and determine our total cash from investments by summing up these line items.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=212)** Next we'll look at our total cash dividends paid.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=215)** Again, this is generally going to be a line item directly from the statement of cash flows.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=221)** It won't appear in other financial statements directly, though it would appear in supporting cash schedules.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=228)** We'll assume a constant level of cash dividends paid.
>
> **[3:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=234)** When we look at issuance and retirement of stock this may be available through the balance sheet but you're more likely to find it in your supporting schedules in another portion of the financial statements.
>
> **[4:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=249)** In our case, we'll assume that we continue to retire stock over time and that we have the same level of debt assurances.
>
> **[4:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=258)** Now of course, these assumptions are solely for learning purposes.
>
> **[4:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=263)** A real company will have differences each year over time.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=267)** We're simply illustrating how you put together these particular statements.
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=272)** Same thing holds true with our FX.
>
> **[4:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=276)** This will be a line item that you'll need to draw from your supporting schedules.
>
> **[4:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=281)** From there, you'll be ready to go through and determine your change in cash over time, and then the resulting beginning and ending cash, which should illustrate a corkscrew effect.
>
> **[4:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=293)** 2015's ending cash is 2016's starting cash and vice versa.
>
> **[4:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=299)** Each year the ending cash becomes the beginning cash for the following year.
>
> **[5:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=305)** Finally, we'll go through and clean up our statements by adding the appropriate lines to make them a little bit easier to read.
>
> **[5:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/setting-source-parameters-2?u=76281980&t=312)** And at this point you now should have a completed set of cash flow statements.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Code Keywords:** continue (2), case, (2), include, (1), finally, (1)
> **CLI Commands:** make (2), find (1)
> **Analogies:** for example (1)
> **Prerequisites:** you'll need (1)
> **Speakers:** - [instructor] (1)

#### Assumptions in financial statements
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Building financial models really starts when we begin making assumptions about what's going to happen to the business over time.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=7)** In particular, in order to get to future assumptions, we're going to have to start by examining what's happened historically.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=14)** I'm in the 02_05_Begin Excel file.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=18)** Now, what we have here are a set of assumptions ranging from assumptions related to TAM, Target Addressable Market, to Income Statement Assumptions and Balance Sheet Assumptions.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=29)** And these are really key assumptions that we're going to need to take from what's happened historically to what's happened in the future in order to forecast where this business will be going.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=40)** Now, each of these assumptions is going to be built on our historical data initially.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=46)** So, for example, looking at Revenue Growth.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=49)** This revenue growth of 5.1% can come from the balance sheet.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=53)** So, if we wanted to understand what 2015 Revenue Growth is, it's simply going to be the difference between our 2015 Revenue and our 2014 Revenue all divided by 2014 Revenue.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=69)** Revenue Growth for 2015 was 7.77%.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=74)** And we can look at this across our entire five year period.
>
> **[1:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=77)** What we see for this particular firm, is that Revenue Growth varies significantly anywhere from mid-double digits down to low single declines in revenue growth.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=90)** Similarly, we'll need to make assumptions about what COGS looks like, what SGNA look like, what Depreciation and Amortization look like and what Interest Rates look like.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=100)** We'll do this based on historical figures from the financial statements.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=106)** That's why, before we can even get to building the assumptions, we need to have an iron clad set of financial statements in place.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=114)** We're going to have the same factors impacting our balance sheet.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=118)** Whether it's Net Receivables based on days, whether it's Inventory, CAP Backs, or Equity Issuance and Debt Issuance, we're going to need to make similar assumptions over time in order to understand what will happen to this firm.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=132)** Finally, and perhaps most difficult of all, we're going to have to make assumptions about what will happen to the market over time.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=141)** Now, in theory, our targeted address we'll market can be broken down into two components.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=146)** How much bigger the pie gets, and then how much bigger our piece of the pie gets.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=151)** We've made an initial statement that in 2014 our piece of the pie grew one percent, while the pie itself grew by seven percent.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=160)** In theory, this should be tied to our Revenue Growth.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=164)** In practice, there will often be some difference between what we calculate as the Market Share growth and our piece of the pie's growth versus what actually happens with our top line.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=176)** Even still, we'll want to go through and make projections based on what's happened over time.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=182)** Now, in our particular case we can't pull these items directly from the financial statements, but we will have to pull them from other data sources.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=192)** So, perhaps as an example, we have a four percent change in the market over time in 2015, and a two percent increase in our share of the market.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=203)** These should tie directly to the level of Revenue Growth.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/assumptions-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=208)** At this point, you should be prepared to go through and begin building out assumptions for your own three statement financial model.

#### Forecasting in financial statements
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Once we've gone through and built out our financial assumptions based on the historical figures, it's time to move on to the forward-looking portion of those assumptions.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=11)** I'm in the 02_06_Begin excel file.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=15)** Now, we've gone through and computed various historical metrics for the firm, revenue growth, cogs as a percentage of revenue, SG&A as a percentage of revenue, etc.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=27)** The point of doing that on a historical basis was not because it was fun, maybe it is, maybe it's not right, but instead, because it sets the ground rules for what we think will happen going forward.
>
> **[0:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=39)** Now there's a few different ways that we could estimate what might happen in the future to this firm.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=46)** Let's just look at revenue growth for example.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=48)** The approach we've taken as a starting point is just to say, let's use the average revenue growth over the last four years.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=57)** In that case, it's 6.3%.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=59)** An alternative approach would be to say, alright, well let's see what we think will happen to say, our market share, based on maybe new products we're rolling out and what we think will happen to the market as a whole, and then we could try to tie our revenue growth to the sum of these two values, and that's okay in practice, but the problem becomes that there's a lot of error that's going to go on in measuring or estimating what our share growth will be and what the overall market growth will be.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=94)** Similarly if we were to simply use the average of the growth over the last four years, we're still going to get a relatively inaccurate picture of what this year's growth is going to be.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=107)** Finally we can just pull a number out of thin air, we could say well based on the data from our salespeople and how we're feeling about things, maybe we think we're going to get an 8% growth rate.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=118)** The point is there's a variety of different ways we can get this projection, we're going to have to pick one.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=123)** Now in our particular case the easiest thing to do is going to be to use average figures over time.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=130)** This has the virtue of being clearly defendable if we should be asked about it by other people and we can do this across most of our different metrics, SG&A, cogs, interest, etc.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=146)** Now certainly, some of these figures will be more forecast-able than others.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=151)** We think about what our interest expense is going to look like.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=154)** This will probably be tied directly to the Fed funds rate and the level of depth that we have maturing.
>
> **[2:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=162)** So we might very well be able to accurately plug in some sort of an estimate there, where it might be much harder to estimate our depreciation or our cogs cost.
>
> **[2:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=174)** When we get done, whatever method we choose, we're going to need to extend this across the entire time period and all of our forward-looking projections.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=186)** The reason for this, is that these assumptions that we're setting now are going to be the basis for our income statement, our balance sheet, and our cash flow statement on a forward-looking basis.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=200)** Given that, it's impossible to be too careful when it comes to establishing the assumptions on a forward-looking basis.
>
> **[3:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=210)** Keep this in mind as you're building up your financial models.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/forecasting-in-financial-statements-2?u=76281980&t=213)** If you're interested in learning more about basic financial forecasting and some of the more advanced methodologies, I recommend you check out my financial forecasting with excel course.

#### Putting it all together
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Once we've made a set of forward-looking assumptions about how we think the firm's revenue, cost and assets and liabilities will change over time, we're prepared to then begin making projections about the firm's financial condition on a forward-looking basis.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=18)** I'm in the 02 07 Begin Excel file.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=23)** Now what we have here are the projections we made around revenue, growth around various firm metrics, etcetera.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=30)** What we want to do is go through and build out the remainder of the income statement.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=35)** We can use the same process to build out the remainder of our balance sheet and cash flow statement.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=42)** So, how do we get started.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=44)** Well begin with we're simply going to take our assumed revenue growth for 2019 and then multiply that by the previous year's revenue.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=53)** We can then extend this out over a five year time horizon.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=57)** Next, we'll want to determine our cost of good sold based on our assumption about COGGS as a percentage of revenue multiplied by the revenue.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=70)** And we can extend this out over five years time.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=72)** We can do the same thing with SG&A, our selling and general administrative expenses.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=78)** Now with other smaller items like R&D, we haven't necessarily made a direct assumption about this.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=84)** Fortunately in this case the firm's R&D appears to be reasonably stable but it is growing over time.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=91)** We might either assume a constant growth rate using a CAGR, compound annual growth rate, or in this case we're using an average based in the last few years.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=102)** We can do the same thing with any sort of unusual expenses, particularly when you start getting to one off items like unusual expenses, these can be very hard to project.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=114)** After all, they are by definition unusual.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=119)** Once we've done all that, we should be able to go through and apply our same Excel formulas to determine our total operating expense and our operating income.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=128)** We could apply the same concept to determine our interest expense based on the historicals and then the earnings before tax.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=140)** Next, we'll need to go through and determine what we expect our income taxes to be.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=144)** This will be based on the income that we earned before tax and the tax rate that we assume over time.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=151)** Now the reality is, items like taxes in the real world should be fairly constant over time.
>
> **[2:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=159)** Sometimes tax rates go up and down because of legislative action or you might have certain tax breaks that we can take advantage of in particular years but this should be a reasonably stable figure and one of the easier ones to project.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=173)** Once we've made those assumptions, we can easily go through and extrapolate what our income taxes will be and then based on that determine our income after taxes using our same formula, of income before taxes less of course the taxes themselves.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=190)** We'll also have extraordinary items which we're just computing based on simple averages over time and then the net income which we determine as a formula.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=200)** Next, I'm going to assume that our weighted average shares for the firm won't change.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=205)** This is probably wrong, but let's face it.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=208)** Almost all of our assumptions are going to be wrong in one way or another.
>
> **[3:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=213)** The key is to make our assumptions as correct as possible.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=217)** Now we could go through and try to tie the weighted average shares over time to any repurchases.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=225)** But the problem is that we still need to know what the expected future stock price is, and that's very difficult to project.
>
> **[3:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=232)** More over I'm going to go through and determine our normalized EPS based on our net income and the weighted average shares.
>
> **[4:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=242)** We would follow a similar procedure to build out the balance sheet and the statement of cash flows.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=248)** At this point though, you should have a good handle on going through and putting together basic financial item projections over time.
>
> **[4:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=256)** The key here is to make sure that you're being careful about what your assumptions are.
>
> **[4:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=262)** Are there any things that stand out to you amongst these assumptions as being a little unusual?
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=267)** One thing that stands out to me, is just looking at our interest as a percentage of long-term debt.
>
> **[4:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=273)** Doesn't look very realistic to have that growing at that kind of rate, right?
>
> **[4:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=276)** So instead, we might want to go through and adjust that over time and the nice thing about Excel, is this will dynamically update across the entire three statement financial model.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/putting-it-all-together-2?u=76281980&t=289)** Now you're all set to make basic financial projections over time for the firm on your own.

#### Improving model quality
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Once you've finished building your three-statement financial model, there are a few things you can check to make sure you have all the right parts and pieces in place.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=8)** To begin with, you want to make sure that you've translated all of your value drivers: price, cost of new capacity, and the cost structure into your financial statement projections appropriately.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=20)** In particular, you need to go through and minimize the operating data so that you have just one measure of capacity and one measure of sales.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=29)** Remember, a financial model is a simplification of reality.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=34)** If you put in too much detail, you're gonna find an overwhelming amount of information, and that'll make it more difficult to make decisions effectively.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=43)** You also need to go through and evaluate the historical relationship between your value drivers and your financial variables.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=51)** So don't just use a generic variable.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=54)** Instead, think about what it is that's really driving those particular sets of relationships.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=61)** It's fine to say that we're just gonna use the average of salary and benefits for the last few years.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=67)** But that's gonna be less accurate than if we can go through and say what is it that drives the change in salary and benefits?
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=75)** Was there a change in minimum wage, for example?
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=78)** Or perhaps we had a major union contract come up for renegotiation at that particular point in time.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=84)** We need to think about what are the real drivers behind the scenes, and that'll let us make more accurate assumptions in the future.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=92)** Remember, there's no generic formula for establishing value drivers.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=97)** Instead, those value drivers need to be based on what's going on in the real world.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=103)** From there you should determine how the financial structure, that is, your outstanding debt, affects financial performance.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=111)** When you're finished, you want to go through and arrange the items in a way that's easy to read.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=116)** So you should have an opening balance sheet.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=119)** And then from there you should have several key items.
>
> **[2:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=122)** You want to make sure that your financial model reports total non-cash current assets, total non-debt current liabilities, total fixed debt to be repaid.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=134)** And all of this needs to be translated into a debt schedule.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=138)** The aggregate of all of your debt issues should tie back to your balance sheet.
>
> **[2:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=143)** You also want to make sure that your history for your revenues, expenses, and depreciation make sense based on what your projections are for the future.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=153)** If historically a firm has grown sales, at say, a 3% rate, and you're projecting that they're suddenly gonna begin growing at a 10% rate, that's probably not gonna be a very accurate financial statement when you get all done.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=166)** Look at what the drivers are in these key items.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=170)** What is it that truly drives revenue behind the scenes?
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=175)** Think about the size of the pie, the size of the overall market, and the amount of market share you have.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=181)** What is it that drives those particular top-line items?
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=186)** You also want to use depreciation, historically, to figure out what your depreciation rate should be going forward.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=193)** Depreciation, while it's a non-cash expense, is still very important to take into account over a long-term financial model, why?
>
> **[3:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=202)** Well, because presumably you're gonna have to reinvest in cap X in the future as that asset becomes more and more worn out.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/improving-model-quality?u=76281980&t=209)** Now, at this point, you have all the information you need to go through and check your own three-statement financial model for completeness.

### 4. 3. Evaluating Corporate Financial Models: Three-Statement Model

#### Financial modeling strategies
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Building out a financial model is not as hard as it seems.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=3)** Let's take a step back and look at the overall process.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=6)** There are six steps in building a financial model.
>
> **[0:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=9)** Step one involves going through and gathering the data that we need to build that model.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=15)** Typically, we're gonna start with our historical financial statements.
>
> **[0:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=19)** So we need to gather them up and then we need to read them and make sure that they make sense.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=24)** Reading them is not as bad as it often seems.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=26)** So if you're not an accounting person and you're adverse to financial information, I recommend you go through and give it a try.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=33)** They're really not as complicated as you might think.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=36)** Second, our next step is to go through and change the arrangement of the financial statements.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=44)** We need to make sure that we've got them arranged, income statement, balance sheet, cash flow statement, and that they make sense from a readability standpoint.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=54)** So we wanna make sure that we're starting with revenue through net income, and that we've linked them together in a readable, usable fashion.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=62)** So have them all in one place, rather than on separate sheets in Excel.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=68)** Step three is to go through and compute our historical ratios based on our past financial statements.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=75)** And then that's gonna give us some kind of mechanical assumption.
>
> **[1:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=78)** For example, looking at accounts receivable to sales or our depreciation rate, or our cost of goods sold to revenue, et cetera.
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=88)** We need to go through and compute those ratios because that gives us a starting point for our assumptions.
>
> **[1:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=94)** Step four is to develop the financial model.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=98)** So we're gonna go through and develop revenue, expenses, and cap ex by working through the different value drivers in the financial model.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=106)** Determine what it is that drives those factors, those business outcomes, and then make sure we're modeling them appropriately.
>
> **[1:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=115)** Once we've got the assumptions in place, we're prepared to finish working through the income statement and then the cash flow statement, and finally the balance sheet.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=124)** We need to make sure that we check that each of these items make sense against one another.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=128)** For example, does the amount of cash on the balance sheet check against the amount of cash generated from the cash flow statement?
>
> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=135)** We need to do that consistently so we make sure there's no errors in our model.
>
> **[2:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=140)** And then step six is to go through and determine the outputs that we care about.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=144)** So for example, valuation or perhaps sensitivity analysis might be the goal in a typical three statement model.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=152)** We wanna understand where the firm is going in the future and what the value of the company might be or the expected net income might be as a result.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=160)** Now, a couple of key best practices to be aware of.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=164)** First of all, I wanna say at the outset, don't be obsessed with best practices.
>
> **[2:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=168)** The reality is it's dangerous to become obsessed with these best practices and models because number one, it can become bureaucratic and a waste of time.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=178)** There are almost always exceptions to best practices out there.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=183)** Next, we wanna make sure that we're going to go through and keep our formulas the same across the financial model.
>
> **[3:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=190)** And that's gonna let us expand that financial model to future years more easily.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=196)** But the reality is that even for something like keeping the formulas the same there can be exceptions if we have the business change.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=204)** If there's, say, a merger and acquisition or another major corporate event.
>
> **[3:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=208)** The point is that we wanna make sure that our model is readable and that we have the appropriate labeling or range names for all of the cells in question.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=217)** In fact, rather than focus on best practices, it's often useful to think about avoiding bad practices.
>
> **[3:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=225)** When we think about what is a bad practice, it's really something that either A, leads to errors in our financial model, or B, makes the financial model more confusing.
>
> **[3:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=235)** So for example, we wanna make sure we avoid long formulas that are difficult to read.
>
> **[4:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=240)** This is probably the single worst problem in financial modeling.
>
> **[4:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=244)** The second big problem that I see is when we don't keep inputs together.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=248)** We wanna make sure that all of our inputs, all of our assumptions are in one place and that they're easy to use, easy to identify, and that they're logically consistent with the financial model as a whole.
>
> **[4:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-modeling-strategies?u=76281980&t=261)** Now you should have a high-level understanding of what's involved in financial modeling and the pitfalls that you wanna avoid when you're building out your model.

#### Sensitivity analysis and financial models
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sensitivity-analysis-and-financial-models-2?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sensitivity-analysis-and-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] If we've built our financial model correctly, when we get done, the whole model should be tied together so that any change to the model dynamically updates across the entire spreadsheet.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sensitivity-analysis-and-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=11)** This is very useful when dealing with practical problems like the need to account for different kinds of scenarios that may arise in corporate finance.
>

>

>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sensitivity-analysis-and-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=57)** But there's nothing magical about that assumption.

>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sensitivity-analysis-and-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=62)** It's simply based on an average of revenue growth over the last four years.
>
> **[1:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sensitivity-analysis-and-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=66)** It's much more realistic to be using specific forecasts for that year, so if we're projecting a minor recession towards the end of 2019 and then a deepening recession that might hit revenues by, say, 9% in 2020 before starting to taper off, what's this going to do to the firm?
>
> **[1:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sensitivity-analysis-and-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=88)** Well, let's take a look.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sensitivity-analysis-and-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=90)** We've gone from having positive revenue growth over time to relatively negative revenue growth.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sensitivity-analysis-and-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=98)** How's this impact our earnings per share?
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sensitivity-analysis-and-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=100)** Well, we go from $3.41 in earnings per share down to $2.84 in 2020.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sensitivity-analysis-and-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=108)** Moreover, the feedback effects over time impact the firm, right?
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sensitivity-analysis-and-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=114)** We see that the firm's growth rate is much weaker than it was before.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sensitivity-analysis-and-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=118)** So in this context, we can go through and we can use single changes about what might happen in the economy such as economic projections to directly determine what we think our forecast earnings will be.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sensitivity-analysis-and-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=134)** Let's pretend that we're betting on a strong rebound after that recession.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sensitivity-analysis-and-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=138)** We've going to have a 6% upgrowth in that year and maybe an additional seven the following year.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sensitivity-analysis-and-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=144)** What's that do to our earnings per share?
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sensitivity-analysis-and-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=146)** Well now, they leap forward towards the end of the period, finishing up $3.35 per share.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/sensitivity-analysis-and-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=152)** Hopefully at this point, you have a better idea how we can go through and adjust our specific assumptions based on individual projections and see how that dynamically flows through the rest of our model.

### 5. 4. Investment Models: DCF Model

#### Financial valuation models
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Business valuation is a common task in the investments world, and a financial model is the typical approach to handling issue.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=7)** In this video, we'll talk about an overview of how valuation models work.
>
> **[0:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=12)** Now a valuation model uses expected cash flows, along with a discount rate and a terminal value, to compute valuation on an asset.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=20)** This could be anything from a particular investment project to an entire company, so when we're talking about project finance, that is a company looking at investing in a specific new asset, be it a new factory as an example, a new piece of equipment, a new, R & D project.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=37)** Valuation models are useful in that scenario.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=40)** If we're looking at evaluating the value of a company as a whole, valuation models are also critical.
>
> **[0:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=47)** The same parts and pieces, the expected future cash flows, the discount rate and the terminal value apply to any type of valuation that we're going to do.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=58)** The specifics will defer of course, but those are the core parts in the valuation model.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=64)** To get started, with a valuation model, you'll need to think about the level of cash flow, that this particular asset is going to generate.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=73)** Choose a level of cash flow that you're comfortable with that you think accurately represents what the company or asset can generate.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=81)** From there, you'll wanna begin using growth rates based on historical figures to assess how that cash flow might change over time.
>
> **[1:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=90)** Once you've done that, you need to pick a discount rate.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=93)** This is probably the hardest part in any valuation because it's the most subjective.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=98)** The discount rate tells us how much we should discount future cash flows when we're figuring out what they're worth today.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=108)** Higher risk projects need higher discount rates.
>
> **[1:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=112)** Now that concept, higher risk projects getting higher discount rates, that's not, in any way controversial.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=118)** The tough part in picking the discount rate is figuring out specifically what that rate should be relative to risk.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=127)** Quantitatively assessing risk is difficult.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=130)** That's a key point to be aware of.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=132)** Once you've gone through and chosen your discount rate and you've forecasted the expected cash flows, perhaps using a three statement model for example, you're prepared to then decide how that growth will change over time.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=145)** Is the growth beyond the level of forecast the cash flow's gonna continue to be constant, is it gonna tail off or even no growth at all.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=153)** If we have say a five year forecast, about what cash flows will be and we're forecasting the specific level of growth in each of those five years, how much will cash flows grow after that five years?
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=167)** Will they continue to grow say constant five percent per year, will it tail off from five to one percent very slowly or will we simply assume that there's no growth at all, beyond the five year period?
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=177)** All of this leads to what we call the terminal value.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=182)** The terminal value is a major part of valuation.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=184)** It's essentially the residual value of the asset after we're done forecasting cash flows, a few years in the future.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=194)** It is often the biggest single part in a valuation model, not always, but often.
>
> **[3:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=200)** Determining what our growth rate assumptions are and our discount rate are critical to the level of the terminal value.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=209)** If we choose our discount rate wrong or we make poor growth assumptions, then our valuation will be completely off.
>
> **[3:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=215)** For that particular asset or business.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/financial-valuation-models?u=76281980&t=218)** At this point, hopefully you have a basic idea of the major inputs that you need to determine in order to create an effective valuation model.
