#### Modeling in banking
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] One of the most common uses for financial models is evaluating credit risk, now and in the future for a particular firm.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=8)** To do that though, you need to understand what credit risk is and the various categories or buckets the firm can fall into.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=15)** In general, credit ratings range from triple A, to D, as in default.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=20)** Nobody fails in credit ratings.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=23)** There's no F category.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=25)** D as in default is the lowest, I like to say.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=28)** Now, there's relatively few triple A firms out there.
>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=31)** So, we'll simply start by talking about double A firms, which represent very low credit risk.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=36)** In general, these are firms that are growing and they have very low levels of leverage.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=42)** They typically have strong positive cash flow generation, and they make consistent dividend payments to their investors.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=49)** Even in a downside case, like a recession, the company should still be able to pay dividends and have strong financial ratios.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=58)** Thus if we're evaluating a financial model and we're trying to see whether a company can maintain a double A credit rating, we'd want to be able to some sort of scenario analysis and find that the company still has more than enough cash to pay dividends, pay debt, and still maintain strong financial ratios.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=76)** In a single A credit rating, the firm is only marginally weaker than a double A credit.
>
> **[1:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=84)** The difference here is that debt leverage can be moderately increasing, perhaps due to acquisitions or capital expenditures.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=93)** In particular, single A credit-rated firms typically have access to debt markets and they have very strong financial ratios based on a healthy business model.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=105)** They're generating more than enough cash, to be able to pay either equity investors or debt investors a healthy and safe rate of return.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=114)** In the triple B space, these are generally moderate risk companies.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=119)** These are firms where they have strong capacitous service debt in the next three years or so, and they probably have modest dividend payments.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=128)** So it's likely that they can survive the next business cycle but we do want to see that in a recession the company, even if they're forced to cut back dividends, they're gonna be able to pay debt and reduce leverage.
>
> **[2:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=142)** So, the key for a moderate risk business, one that has little more risk versus the low-risk firms that we talked about earlier, they have greater levels of leverage and perhaps they're not growing as strong, they're not generating as much cash, but they still have more than enough money, especially if they cut back on equity dividends to be able to meet their obligations.
>
> **[2:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=163)** In the high risk space, double B companies have tight, but positive debt service coverage for at least the next two years.
>
> **[2:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=172)** In general, these are firms that typically have very volatile cash flows and high leverage.
>
> **[2:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=177)** So, they don't have a lot of discretionary cash flow.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=179)** And in a recession, that leverage will probably increase, and the company is going to have weak financial ratios.
>
> **[3:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=186)** Overall though, there's no indication the company is going to go bankrupt in a non-downside, non-recessionary setting.
>
> **[3:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=194)** Very high risk firms, with a single B credit rating, are those where there's substantial concern about their ability to generate cash flow even if the economic environment remains strong.
>
> **[3:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=207)** This firm may have to cut costs in order to maintain their debt service.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=211)** They're probably not going to be making dividend payments and they typically are very highly levered.
>
> **[3:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=217)** Of course, it's difficult to be a safe company.
>
> **[3:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=222)** It's hard to maintain the kind of strong credit ratings that investors like to see.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=228)** It's much easier to be a high risk company, but the purpose in financial modeling, when it comes to risk evaluation, is to look at not where the company is today, but where it might be in the future, based on these metrics.
>
> **[4:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=243)** How well the company is servicing its debt.
>
> **[4:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=246)** How well the company is rewarding equity investors and the level of free cash flow the company has in comparison to those needs.
>
> **[4:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-banking?u=76281980&t=254)** Now you're all set to begin breaking firms down into different groupings based on their credit risk as exemplified in a financial model.

#### Modeling in corporate finance
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-corporate-finance?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-corporate-finance?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The two major areas of finance are corporate finance and investments.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-corporate-finance?u=76281980&t=5)** Financial modeling is important in both areas.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-corporate-finance?u=76281980&t=8)** In the corporate finance world, we care primarily about the cash flow statement, the income statement, and the balance sheet.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-corporate-finance?u=76281980&t=16)** But, we want to use these pieces of accounting information as the basis for financial models that we build to answer finance questions.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-corporate-finance?u=76281980&t=27)** Questions around valuation, questions around risk, questions around investments that the company might make.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-corporate-finance?u=76281980&t=35)** We're gonna begin any corporate finance model by taking the historical financials, and then making assumptions about what the drivers are of those financials.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-corporate-finance?u=76281980&t=45)** What are the drivers of sales, of costs, and of profitability?
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-corporate-finance?u=76281980&t=51)** We can then distill those drivers down in a financial model, and that allows us to go through and begin creating the different components in the financial model.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-corporate-finance?u=76281980&t=61)** In particular, any corporate finance model needs to have four main areas: some sort of an analysis of revenue and expenses, some sort of an analysis of working capital, a debt schedule, and a fixed asset schedule.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-corporate-finance?u=76281980&t=79)** All four of these separate parts come together to allow us to make decisions about what the company as a whole should do.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-corporate-finance?u=76281980&t=87)** By combining revenue and expense analysis with an understanding of working capital, the debts, and the assets that the firm has, that is income statement items with balance sheet items, we can then determine what the profit and loss for the company are, and what level of interest the company is gonna be paying on its debt.
>
> **[1:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-corporate-finance?u=76281980&t=105)** After taking into account interest and the other costs we face, then, we can compute what the taxes will be for the firm.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-corporate-finance?u=76281980&t=113)** And that lets us go through and forecast cash balances, debt balances, and then the surplus cash that we'll have to reward equity shareholders.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-corporate-finance?u=76281980&t=125)** We can put all of this together into a free cash flow metric that we use as part of the balance sheet, the income statement, and the cash flow statement to forecast what'll happen to the firm going forward.
>
> **[2:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-corporate-finance?u=76281980&t=138)** A good financial model addresses all of these primary corporate finance concerns.

#### Modeling in investments
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-investments?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-investments?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Financial modeling is an extremely important skill in the investments world.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-investments?u=76281980&t=5)** Let's face it. At the end of the day, most of the investment's work comes down to analyzing whether it makes sense to purchase a particular asset at a particular price or not.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-investments?u=76281980&t=16)** This is an area where financial modeling shines.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-investments?u=76281980&t=20)** So what do you need to do in order to build an effective investment model?
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-investments?u=76281980&t=24)** Well, there are a few different types of information that you'll need.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-investments?u=76281980&t=28)** To begin with, you're gonna start by looking at the asset in question, and you're gonna look at what kind of cash flows it generates.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-investments?u=76281980&t=36)** So look at the transaction you're proposing and the sources and uses of cash analysis.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-investments?u=76281980&t=43)** From there you'll be able to move on to examine the balance sheet and goodwill of that particular investment.
>
> **[0:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-investments?u=76281980&t=52)** You'll need to go through and identify the financials that the target company or target investment has as well as the financials that the purchaser has.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-investments?u=76281980&t=63)** Does the purchaser have the wherewithal to purchase this particular asset?
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-investments?u=76281980&t=67)** Combining sources and uses with the financials for the acquiring company and the target company let's us go through and evaluate how much debt we'll need to issue in order to purchase this particular investment, if any, and whether or not we'll be able to have the appropriate level of financing in place for that debt.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-investments?u=76281980&t=87)** From there we'll be able to go through and evaluate whether the investment in question will throw off enough cash to justify the investment.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-investments?u=76281980&t=99)** That let's us go through, from a financial modeling perspective, and evaluate certain outputs of interest.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-investments?u=76281980&t=106)** What is the value of this particular investment, either on an enterprise basis or a per share basis, perhaps?
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-investments?u=76281980&t=114)** What is the level of credit quality of this particular investment?
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-investments?u=76281980&t=118)** And how does that translate to risk?
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/modeling-in-investments?u=76281980&t=121)** Is this an investment that we're prepared to take on given the level of risk that the financial statements reflect?

### 9. 8. Building and Maintaining Models

#### Applications of financial models
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Financial models have many business applications and knowing where to use them is just as important as knowing how to build them.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=7)** The fundamental issue in any evaluation model is how to assess the risk of future cash flow projections.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=15)** Think about an example with a stock that trades in the market.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=20)** Let's pretend that stock ABC is trading at $60 per share.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=26)** Well, we might say, based on financial theory, we want to own stock ABC.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=30)** It helps us to diversify our portfolio overall and looks like a solid company.
>
> **[0:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=35)** That's great but we still don't know whether we should actually buy the stock based on its current price of $60 per share.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=42)** So we can turn to a mathematical model.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=45)** Some sort of a computation to evaluate whether or not this stock is undervalued or overvalued, and maybe our mathematical model suggests that stock ABC is worth $30 per share.
>
> **[1:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=60)** The problem is that the mathematical model is not taking into account what's actually going on in the markets themselves, the practical market information that's out there.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=70)** It's not taking into account things like, what is the prevailing P/E ratio in the market?
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=75)** Instead, we need to take into account what the mathematical model says and combine that with practical market information to build a comprehensive, overall financial model.
>
> **[1:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=87)** Using that financial model then, we can take into account both the valuation from a mathematical perspective and the existing market trends and make a decision about that investment.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=102)** Now, there are five different areas where we're most likely to need a financial model.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=109)** The first is a DCF, or discounted cash flow analysis.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=113)** We're typically gonna use a DCF model to value a business or another asset of some sort.
>
> **[1:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=119)** And so, what we're really doing is taking our theoretical model and we're trying to put actual practical values, based on what's going on in the market, into that DCF model to make a decision whether we should buy or sell that particular investment.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=137)** Similarly, and M&A analysis lets us go through and evaluate the attractiveness of a potential merger or acquisition target, or a divestiture of one our business segments.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=148)** The third type of area where we might need a financial model is in capital raising.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=152)** So for example, we might be interested in analyzing the pro forma impact of raising debt or equity or other kinds of capital events.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=161)** We might asks ourselves okay, given what's going on in markets as a whole, does it make sense to raise capital in order to expand the firm in order to pursue new growth opportunities or new investments?
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=173)** A financial model can help us make this decision.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=176)** A fourth area where we might see the need for a financial model is in LBO analysis.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=182)** So if we're working for a private equity firm we might ask, well how much leverage can we use to purchase a company?
>
> **[3:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=189)** How much debt can we use to buy out the equity of that company, to try to improve its operations, and earn a return?
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=197)** And then the fifth and perhaps most common area where you might want to use a financial model is in sensitivity analysis.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=205)** We're gonna be interested in not only a go-no-go decision around the financial model but looking at how confident we are in that go-no-go decision.
>
> **[3:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=216)** In other words, if are assumptions prove to be incorrect, we need to be able to evaluate whether the decision still makes sense in the context of weaker or stronger assumptions.
>
> **[3:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=229)** If our growth projections prove too optimistic, and we instead loosen those growth projections, so we're now growing at a slower pace, does it still make sense to pursue this particular investment?
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/applications-of-financial-models?u=76281980&t=241)** That's what financial modeling is all about.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Env Vars:** abc (3), dcf (3), lbo (1)
> **CLI Commands:** make (5)
> **Code Keywords:** let (1), raise (1), private (1)
> **Definitions:** is a  (1), in other words (1)
> **Analogies:** for example (1)
> **Speakers:** - [instructor] (1)

#### Bitcoin and cryptocurrency valuation modeling
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] One of the fun things about financial models is the ability to attack problems in order to make decisions that other people are confused about.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=8)** One great example of this is is in the widely discussed bitcoin and cryptocurrency space.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=15)** There's a lot of discussion, at present, in the financial markets about what these cryptocurrencies, including bitcoin, are worth, if anything.
>
> **[0:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=23)** A financial model can help us drill down on that issue.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=27)** Let me show you what I'm referring to.
>
> **[0:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=29)** So, this is a rather sophisticated, or advanced financial model, but it's different than many of the models that we've talked about thus far.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=37)** In particular, we're looking at an investment in an intangible asset, in this case the bitcoin, and we're trying to understand what it'll be worth in the future.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=49)** Well, regardless of the fact that bitcoin is very different from say a factory or a company, it's nonetheless an asset that we can model effectively using the same kinds of techniques we've been talking about all along.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=64)** So, in this particular scenario, we've gone through and developed five different methods for valuing bitcoin, each with their own separate section in the financial model.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=75)** We have the world wealth approach, which looks at the value of bitcoin as a percentage of world currency over time.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=83)** The wallet value approach, which looks at the value of bitcoin based on the number of cryptocurrency wallets there are out there.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=91)** The mining profit approach, which looks at the value of bitcoin based on the number of miners.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=97)** The miner cost approach, which looks at the value of bitcoin based on the cost to mine it.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=103)** And the alternative coin approach, which looks at the value of bitcoin based on competition from other cryptocurrencies that are out there.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=111)** Now, we have separate schedules related to this particular financial model and the data that we've gathered as it relates to bitcoin.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=121)** So, we have information about mining schedules, wallet growth, etc.
>
> **[2:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=126)** And the point here is not to say that this is the gospel truth for bitcoin's value or anything of the sort.
>
> **[2:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=132)** Instead, it's to illustrate how we can use a financial model to put a value on something that's otherwise very confusing.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=141)** In point of fact, when we look at the value of bitcoin under each of these scenarios, our approach is very similar.
>
> **[2:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=150)** Figure out what the value of one bitcoin will be in a particular year, over the next few years and then, figure out the current value of that particular bitcoin based on the approach.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=165)** From there we use a weighting scheme to determine the effective value of each bitcoin based on the weight we assign to the valuation methodology.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=178)** So, the miner's cost is an example, the miner's profit, and the alternative coin approach all get 17.5% weights, the wallet value approach gets a 40% weight, and the world wealth approach gets a 7.5% weight.
>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=192)** When we take all of these factors into account, we get a single value for bitcoin each year for the next six years running.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=203)** Putting that all together then, we come up with the present value of bitcoin which we project to be $12,274.34 using a roughly 31% discount rate.
>
> **[3:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/bitcoin-and-cryptocurrency-valuation-modeling?u=76281980&t=218)** Now, this is a great example of complex financial modeling being used to attack a problem which is otherwise extremely complicated and difficult to analyze using more conventional and simpler techniques like a typical multiple approach used by some investment analysts.

> [!info]- Semantic Content

#### Updating financial models
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/updating-financial-models-2?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/updating-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The reality is that over time all financial models will need to be updated.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/updating-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=5)** Projected revenues will become actual revenues and we'll have to generate new projections down the road.
>
> **[0:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/updating-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=11)** I'm in the 08_03_Begin Excel file.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/updating-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=15)** Now what we have here is Microsoft stock and financial information starting in the first quarter of 2014 all the way through the second quarter of 2018.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/updating-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=27)** But let's hypothetically pretend that we fast forward six months and now we need to update Microsoft's financials based on what's happened over the next couple of quarters.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/updating-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=40)** Well, to do this, we'll simply assume a random but reasonable set of additional numbers and so, I'm going to go through and multiply each of our figures by say a 5% growth rate.
>
> **[0:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/updating-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=58)** And that'll give us an updated set of financials.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/updating-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=62)** The point isn't of course that the 5% is exactly right, instead this just emphasizes that we would need to be able to go through and adjust the base information we have.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/updating-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=74)** From there we then need to adjust all of our inputs in the models that rely on that information.
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/updating-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=81)** So, for example, if we're trying to determine the fair value of Microsoft stock, we need to make sure that we're operating on the most recent available information.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/updating-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=91)** If we don't, then we risk our model being incorrect over time.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/updating-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=97)** Once we've gone through and adjusted this model based on the most recent information, we'll have a better ability to talk with management or other stakeholders about what the future might hold.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/updating-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=107)** The point is if we're constructed our model correctly, this should be a quick and simple process just like you saw here.

> [!info]- Semantic Content
>
> **Code Keywords:** let (1), this, (1)
> **Analogies:** for example (1), just like (1)

#### Maintaining ongoing financial models
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] In addition to building new financial models, it's equally important to be able to go through and maintain existing financial models.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=7)** Oftentimes, this includes the need to update the model as new results come in, and also to explain to management and other stakeholders what those new results mean compared to the projections we made in the model.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=22)** I'm in the 08_04.Begin Excel file.
>
> **[0:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=26)** Now what we have here is our three-statement model, where we've updated 2018 to include 2019 actuals, but we've left in the 2019 Estimates column.
>
> **[0:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=40)** What we're essentially looking to do is go through and understand how our projections performed against what actually happened in the model.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=48)** To do this, we've created a new column over here on the far-right, called the Variance to Plan.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=54)** Variance to Plan simply refers to the difference between the actual results we achieved compared to what we planned to achieve or expected to achieve.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=64)** These types of variances are very common for companies to examine and focus on on an annual and even quarterly basis.
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=74)** In fact, variance analysis is a key part of FP&A, Financial Planning and Analysis, which is part of most corporate finance functions.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=83)** To determine that variance, we're simply going to take the plan figure minus the actual and subtract the two, and this tells us that our Plan to Actual on revenue, for example, was 16,272.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=102)** We intended to come in 16,272 higher on revenue than we really needed.
>
> **[1:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=109)** Now in this case, all of our figures are in thousands of dollars, so this would equate to a $16.27 million shortfall.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=118)** We could do the same thing across our entire income statement to get a sense for how the firm performed during this period.
>
> **[2:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=129)** And most important of all, when we get it all done, we could go through and evaluate how this impacted the bottom line.
>
> **[2:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=137)** Now notice, the way that these numbers are reported is based on which number we subtract first.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=145)** In this case, we're doing Plan to Actual.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=148)** So we've taken Plan minus Actual.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=151)** It might be more effective if we were to think about it in the opposite direction, because we've had a shortfall here; we've missed estimates.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=160)** Thus, maybe we should be thinking about Actual to Plan.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=164)** If we want to approach it that way, and neither way is more correct than the other, it's just a matter of interpretation, we can go through and adjust our Variance column based on those figures, and this gives us a little better interpretation of how we did.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=183)** So in this case, we see we had a $16.2 million shortfall, which translated to a bottom line decrease in earnings per share of $0.16 versus our plan.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/maintaining-ongoing-financial-models-2?u=76281980&t=196)** Now you're ready to go through and construct basic variances for our own financial models.

### 10. Conclusion

#### Next steps
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/next-steps?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/next-steps?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Michael] I hope you've enjoyed the course and it's given you a practical understanding of what's needed in a typical financial modeling project.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/next-steps?u=76281980&t=8)** Throughout this course we've learned about the three major types of financial models and the work and effort required to develop those models.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/next-steps?u=76281980&t=17)** The first model we talked about was the three-statement model.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/next-steps?u=76281980&t=20)** This gave us a picture on what the future of a particular company looked like based on the income statement, the balance sheet, and the cashflow statement.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/next-steps?u=76281980&t=30)** We saw how to make projections based on each of those three sheets and how the forecast of a problem was coming for the company down the road.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/next-steps?u=76281980&t=38)** The second type of model we reviewed was the discounted cashflow model.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/next-steps?u=76281980&t=42)** This was useful for valuing companies and assets and giving us a clear indication of whether or not we should pursue a particular investment, be it as an investor or a company.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/next-steps?u=76281980&t=54)** The third type of model that we looked at were buyout models.
>
> **[0:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/next-steps?u=76281980&t=57)** These models are often used in investment banking and by investment bankers advising clients looking at mergers and acquisition deals.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/next-steps?u=76281980&t=67)** As you move forward in your career, I recommend you keep a couple of things in mind.
>
> **[1:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/next-steps?u=76281980&t=72)** First of all, keep practicing and learn new tools.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/next-steps?u=76281980&t=75)** Financial modeling is always evolving, and while you now have all of the foundations that you need to be an effective modeler, there's always more to learn.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/next-steps?u=76281980&t=86)** To that end, I recommend three great courses here on LinkedIn learning: Financial Forecasting with Big Data, Algorithmic Trading and Stock Essentials Training, and Pricing Analytics for Corporate Finance Essential Training.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/next-steps?u=76281980&t=100)** Each of these courses relates closely to applied financial models that we've talked about throughout this course.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/next-steps?u=76281980&t=108)** Thanks for participating.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/financial-modeling-foundations-2018/next-steps?u=76281980&t=110)** I wish you the best of luck in your financial modeling journey.
